#### [Clustering](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/advanced-tableau-desktop/clustering?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/advanced-tableau-desktop/clustering?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Clustering is a method of partitioning observations or marks into clusters around the nearest mean, also known as a centroid. Observations within clusters are more similar to each other than those in the other clusters. [Tableau](../../Skills/Data%20Science/Tableau.md) utilizes K means clustering, also known as the centroidic model. This model is characterized by using a single mean per cluster, which is an average of all values inside each cluster. Clustering is valuable for grouping like observations for later analysis. This can be very helpful for large data sets or a pattern may not be readily visible. Clustering is often used as a pre-processing or initial observation point for other predictive analytic processes. Adding a cluster inside Tableau is very straightforward. You'll go to the analytics tab, you'll drag out cluster and you'll drop it in the view. As far as cluster customization is concerned, you'll have two primary controls. Those include variables and your number of clusters. Variables represent the fields Tableau uses to compute clusters. You can add or remove variables to adjust clusters. Note that in the describe clusters dialogue box, variable value grouping can be reviewed before modifying the cluster variables. The number of clusters will be determined automatically. This uses the Calinski-Harabasz criterion
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/advanced-tableau-desktop/clustering?u=76281980&t=95)** unless explicitly defined by the user. Note that if a categorical value, aka a dimension has more than 25 unique values, it'll be disregarded in the cluster calculation even if you drag it into your variables. A quick pro tip around clustering, you can drag the cluster bill from the marks card to the data pane to create a cluster group that can be used in other sheets. Just refit the data leverage in your cluster and you're good to go. Now that we've reviewed how to add a cluster and customize a cluster, let's leverage clustering inside our own workbook. So we're going to call this average pick duration
>
> **[9:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/advanced-tableau-desktop/clustering?u=76281980&t=570)** by location and we'll bold the by location again, size 11, like everything else, right click that and we're going to add that same gray background right there, the light gray right there so it matches everything else here. And then we'll go into our sheet. And instead of coloring by the sum of boxes picked, we're actually going to cover color by the average of boxes picked. And then we'll pop back into the dashboard and see how that looks. And now we're going to actually change which measure we're leveraging in this view for the color. So we're going to drag out pick duration, we're going to drop that on color and we're going to line that up to be the average pick duration. Then we'll go ahead and we'll change our color. We're going to change this to our orange blue diverging, and we'll do a reverse because our pick duration as it gets higher, that's not good. As it gets lower, that's better. So we'll hit okay there and then we'll just push our good and bad colors around a little bit. 'Cause we don't want everything to look completely bad, then we won't be able to tell what's good and what's bad. So let's just modify our center to be about 2.2 minutes. We'll hit apply there. That's looking a bit better. Let's, let's bump it up to 2.5 and see how that looks. All right, so the key point is here, we really want to get the outliers, the bad points kind of highlighted. And everything else that meets our threshold, we're going to leave and we'll concentrate on the worst offenders first.
>
> **[11:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/advanced-tableau-desktop/clustering?u=76281980&t=667)** And we changed this to average pick duration 'cause that's really turned into our overwhelming metric for the [rest](../../Skills/Web%20Development/Representational%20State%20Transfer%20(REST).md) of our views in our advanced analytics warehouse analytics section. So let's go ahead and just remove that legend there. And this is looking pretty nice. Our last piece here is we're going to go ahead and use this sheet as a filter for the rest of the sheets in our view as we're going to want to select on a specific picker. And we're going to drill down and do analysis just for that picker. So let's go ahead and just drag our title down a tiny bit 'cause we're losing it a tiny bit and that's not good for our end user. They're not going to know which metrics they're looking at. So let's go ahead and just drag the title down until we get a nice wrap on two lines. And it looks like we clicked on the first picker and all of our analytics changed, which is exactly what we want. And if we look, yes, there it is, our R squared is looking a bit better. And our P value is looking great for this specific individual. So that means our trend is a little bit better, our predictions, which is awesome. And that's exactly what we thought would happen as we drill down into each individual. So that wraps up our internal tool lessons. Now we're going to move on to our external tool lessons. And first up we're going to look at R and [Python](../../Skills/Software%20Development/Python%20(Programming%20Language).md) integration inside Tableau.

#### [R and Python integration](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/advanced-tableau-desktop/r-python-integration?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/advanced-tableau-desktop/r-python-integration?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Presenter] R and [Python](../../Skills/Software%20Development/Python%20(Programming%20Language).md) are popular programming languages for performing complex statistical analyses. Both R and Python functions and models can be used inside [Tableau](../../Skills/Data%20Science/Tableau.md) via calculated fields. There are several steps required to utilize both platforms in combination with Tableau. These include installing the platform, installing the server, connecting to your service, and adding your calculated fields. Note that both sets of calculated fields will both start with script inside Tableau, whether you're using R or Python. These script calculations will essentially call functions from the related servers. It's important to remember that R and Python are complex languages, which require a base level proficiency to be utilized inside Tableau. Tableau leverages calculated fields to run R and Python scripts, but users should know the languages first to effectively utilize R and Python inside Tableau. Additionally, installation and configuration will vary widely, this combined with the background knowledge required for the functions and scripts to be leveraged are the primary reasons why we are not going to fully delve into these tools in this course. These tools are so powerful and complex that they could dictate entire courses in their own right. It's strongly encouraged that if you wish to utilize either tool, you do research on them independent of Tableau
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/advanced-tableau-desktop/r-python-integration?u=76281980&t=94)** prior to integration. These are tremendously powerful tools and have the potential to truly up your game when presenting [Predictive Analytics](../../Skills/Data%20Science/Predictive%20Analytics.md) inside Tableau. Next up, we'll provide an overview of dashboard extensions inside Tableau Desktop.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Frameworks & Libraries:** [Tableau](../../Skills/Data%20Science/Tableau.md) (9), [Python](../../Skills/Software%20Development/Python%20(Programming%20Language).md) (6), [Predictive Analytics](../../Skills/Data%20Science/Predictive%20Analytics.md) (1)

#### [Dashboard extensions](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/advanced-tableau-desktop/dashboard-extensions?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/advanced-tableau-desktop/dashboard-extensions?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Dashboard Extensions are web applications created by [Tableau](../../Skills/Data%20Science/Tableau.md) partners, designed to help users customize and enhance their standard [Dashboards](../../Skills/Data%20Science/Dashboards.md). Adding an extension is fairly straightforward. First, you'll download the extension from the Extension Gallery. Second, you'll add your extension to My Tableau Repository. Each extension will have the file type .trex. Once this is complete, you can add to your dashboard just by clicking and dragging the extension object into your view. Once this is complete, you can configure the extension to your liking. Now, while extensions can broaden the analytic capabilities and functionality of Tableau, it should be noted that there are some caveats to leveraging them. First, most Tableau Extensions do not work with Tableau Public as of yet, so for those looking to leverage public extensions, your ability to do so will be limited. Second, while there are some free extensions within the Gallery, most require a subscription or a purchase of some sort to be able to enable the functionality behind the extension. Finally, many extensions require at least an aggregate amount of data to be pulled back and maintained or manipulated on a third-party platform. This can be a limiting barrier, especially inside large organizations which may have strict [Data Sharing](../../Skills/Database%20Management/Data%20Sharing.md) policies. Before leveraging extensions, please ensure that you've checked out all legal and security restrictions and concerns.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/advanced-tableau-desktop/dashboard-extensions?u=76281980&t=94)** We encourage you to look at the Extension Gallery to see if any existing extensions provide deeper functionality that your company may benefit from.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Frameworks & Libraries:** [Tableau](../../Skills/Data%20Science/Tableau.md) (5), [Dashboards](../../Skills/Data%20Science/Dashboards.md) (1), [Data Sharing](../../Skills/Database%20Management/Data%20Sharing.md) (1)

The World Health Organization has been generating significant press for a recent study on global life expectancy and has asked you to help conduct some statistical modeling and predictive analysis to better understand the data. For this project, you'll need to apply predictive analytic tools in [Tableau](../../Skills/Data%20Science/Tableau.md) to explore trends, build forecasts, and conduct a cluster analysis using the WHO life expectancy dataset. Your job is to find key nuggets of information to help guide the team as they target regions to investigate in their future research. Your objective is to use Tableau Desktop to create trends to identify patterns in the data, leverage forecasts to project future data points, and apply clustering to segment WHO data. This is your last homework for this course, so best of luck and get busy.
